    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_981119917" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/981119917" />
    <a title="Anna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14941179-anna"><img alt="Anna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1353981100p2/14941179.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/981119917?book_show_action=true">Jun 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anna" href="/user/show/14941179-anna">Anna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780199537471" href="/book/show/6250391-the-ragged-trousered-philanthropists">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14941179-anna?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14941179-anna?shelf=poverty">poverty</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14941179-anna?shelf=politics">politics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer981119917" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11944714347925660517">‘The Ragged-Trousered Philanthropists’ is a wonderful, depressing book. Not surprisingly, it reminded me of Jack London’s <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/113250.The_People_of_the_Abyss' title='The People of the Abyss by Jack London' rel='nofollow noopener'>The People of the Abyss</a>, which similarly demonstrated the terrible plight of the poor in Edwardian England. The two differ, however, in that London focused on the city poor and presented his book as reportage. Tressell’s book centres around a town (a thinly veiled portrait of Hastings) and is told as a novel. Both are polemics, showing the reader the appalling suffering that </span>
  <span id="freeText11944714347925660517" style="display:none">‘The Ragged-Trousered Philanthropists’ is a wonderful, depressing book. Not surprisingly, it reminded me of Jack London’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/113250.The_People_of_the_Abyss" title="The People of the Abyss by Jack London" rel="nofollow noopener">The People of the Abyss</a>, which similarly demonstrated the terrible plight of the poor in Edwardian England. The two differ, however, in that London focused on the city poor and presented his book as reportage. Tressell’s book centres around a town (a thinly veiled portrait of Hastings) and is told as a novel. Both are polemics, showing the reader the appalling suffering that free market capitalism inflicts upon the worst off. Notably, Tressell also examines how those most harmed by the system are unable and unwilling to criticise it - they have been taught to believe that the rich are their betters and that they deserve no more than they get. The difficulty of bringing others round to the socialist cause is a particular theme.<br /><br />The introduction (which, as ever, I read last) provides an excellent analysis of the context and history of the book. Tressell died before it was published, initially in a highly abbreviated form, and it’s sheer luck that the manuscript survived at all. The novel recounts a year in the life of working families in ‘Mugsborough’, including all ages, men, women, children, rich, poor, starving, religious, socialist, and neither. Although Tressell is evidently writing to advance the cause of socialism, the writing is powerful enough for the lectures included within it never to pall. The fates of various characters are also very upsetting, as the working families are always insecure, with one piece of bad luck enough to precipitate starvation. Despite this, the book has an excellent sense of humour (although the naming scheme is a little heavy-handed) and an eye for dark ironies.<br /><br />I think it important that books like this and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/113250.The_People_of_the_Abyss" title="The People of the Abyss by Jack London" rel="nofollow noopener">The People of the Abyss</a> are still read. The current political narratives of austerity and reducing the welfare safety net carefully ignore the appalling state of affairs before such a safety net existed. Without any protection from arbitrary redundancy, no support for children and the elderly, and nothing to live on if you had no work, people starved. As the 19th century became the 20th, England was seen as a rich, mighty power, proud of its empire and so far unhumbled by world war. Yet a huge proportion of the population lived in squalor, ill-health, and poverty. The rise of zero hours contracts, the housing crisis, and increasing inequality, amongst other trends, suggest that the 21st century we are backsliding. Tressell’s conception of socialism is well-articulated, if a bit dated, and certainly reminded me of the ongoing structural problems with free market capitalism. The bitter critique of Christianity and its hypocrisy was also very interesting. Although this could have been a fatalistic book, it isn’t. The ending is moving and I won’t soon forget Owen, Philpot, Bert, et al. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11944714347925660517" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('GV67zPnlOOu42J4TD0pXj4KINmXSLQdeJTAVLUyatHLrcug2Mx++WxDZWtNdFGDqNFZgyd1jeENmFnnF6iQguw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('TdjBvlXLQ0tqVhwicTTob0V6fWAmGH9vd4fSFVAa7AK/9JJEnzHF+8JX2OIjat8K86QrzClWAHI0ob799qR4yw==')})
  }

Then, in 2008, on the brink of collapse after lending too much money to mortgage-hungry customers, Northern Rock was saved in the largest bank bail-out in history. But why, over one hundred years later, did the Bank of England change tack and intervene?The answer is that, in the years between 1886 and 2008, the UK economy had transformed, and was now more reliant on banks than ever before -- without them, almost every area of economic activity would have ground to a halt. This signifies a fundamental change in the UK\'s economic model, and this fundamental change has a name: financialisation.Stolen tells the story of how and why this financialisation occurred, what it means for our society and politics, and what the left can do to fight it. At present, the odds are stacked against labour and in favour of finance capital. But what follows it will be determined by which group - the many or the few - manages to take power in this moment of crisis. How we understand this moment, and what we do with it, will determine the course of the future.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"12528176994060237867\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return Its success &quot;might have established communal property, a far wider democracy in political and legal institutions, might have disestablished the state church and rejected the protestant ethic.&quot; \n\nIn The World Turned Upside Down, Christopher Hill studies the beliefs of such radical groups as the Diggers, the Ranters, the Levellers and others, and the social and emotional impulses that gave rise to them. \n\nThe relations between rich and poor classes, the part played by wandering \'masterless men,\' the outbursts of sexual freedom and deliberate blasphemy, the great imaginative creations of Milton and Bunyan - these and many other elements build up into a marvellously detailed and coherent portrait of this strange, sudden effusion of revolutionary beliefs. It is a portrait not of the bourgeois revolution that actually took place, but of the impulse towards a far more fundamental overturning of society.\n\n&quot;Incorporates some of Dr. Hill\'s most Knight long wrestled with what it means to be savedwhat God can do for us and in us.This book in many ways is the result of that personal search: the combination of biblical findings, scholarly studies, and encounters with Christians. <span id="freeTextContainer12793387147982808579">Robert Tressell (pen name used by Robert Noonan; April 17, 1870—February 3, 1911) was an Irish-British writer best known for his novel The Ragged Trousered Philanthropists.<br/><br/></span>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/906396-ragged-trousered-philanthropists">Quotes from The Ragged Trouse...</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Poverty is not caused by men and women getting married; it's not caused by machinery; it's not caused by "over-production"; it's not caused by drink or laziness; and it's not caused by "over-population". It's caused by Private Monopoly. That is the present system. They have monopolized everything that it is possible to monopolize; they have got the whole earth, the minerals in the earth and the streams that water the earth. The only reason they have not monopolized the daylight and the air is that it is not possible to do it. If it were possible to construct huge gasometers and to draw together and compress within them the whole of the atmosphere, it would have been done long ago, and we should have been compelled to work for them in order to get money to buy air to breathe. And if that seemingly impossible thing were accomplished tomorrow, you would see thousands of people dying for want of air - or of the money to buy it - even as now thousands are dying for want of the other necessities of life. You would see people going about gasping for breath, and telling each other that the likes of them could not expect to have air to breathe unless the had the money to pay for it. Most of you here, for instance, would think and say so. Even as you think at present that it's right for so few people to own the Earth, the Minerals and the Water, which are all just as necessary as is the air. In exactly the same spirit as you now say: "It's Their Land," "It's Their Water," "It's Their Coal," "It's Their Iron," so you would say "It's Their Air," "These are their gasometers, and what right have the likes of us to expect them to allow us to breathe for nothing?" And even while he is doing this the air monopolist will be preaching sermons on the Brotherhood of Man; he will be dispensing advice on "Christian Duty" in the Sunday magazines; he will give utterance to numerous more or less moral maxims for the guidance of the young. And meantime, all around, people will be dying for want of some of the air that he will have bottled up in his gasometers. And when you are all dragging out a miserable existence, gasping for breath or dying for want of air, if one of your number suggests smashing a hole in the side of one of th gasometers, you will all fall upon him in the name of law and order, and after doing your best to tear him limb from limb, you'll drag him, covered with blood, in triumph to the nearest Police Station and deliver him up to "justice" in the hope of being given a few half-pounds of air for your trouble.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/284151-poverty-is-not-caused-by-men-and-women-getting-married">68 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Every man who is not helping to bring about a better state of affairs for the future is helping to perpetuate the present misery, and is therefore the enemy of his own children. There is no such thing as being neutral: we must either help or hinder.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/7867483-every-man-who-is-not-helping-to-bring-about-a">13 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
        <a class="actionLink" style="float: right" href="/work/quotes/906396-ragged-trousered-philanthropists">More quotes&hellip;</a>
<div class="clear"></div></div></div><div class="bigBoxBottom"></div></div>
